Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Importance of Islamic Methodology
Foreword discussing the need for an Islamic methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the central message of the foreword: the need for a distinctive Islamic methodology and the intellectual currents it opposed.

Core Idea
Methodology is the lens through which knowledge is evaluated; Islam has its own.

In this foreword, the writer explains the significance of the book and highlights the author's lifelong mission: to establish awareness of a distinct Islamic methodology. This lesson helps you grasp why methodology matters and what the author sought to counter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's goal
Read the passage to find what the author aimed to instill in his students. Look for phrases like 'غرس الوعي بالمنهج' (to instill awareness of methodology).
2
Recognize the opposing currents
Identify the two trends dominant at the time: one claiming Muslims had no distinct methodology (only Greek), and another reconciling Islam with Indian, Persian, and Pharaonic roots.
3
Understand the implications
Why was it problematic that some denied an Islamic methodology? How did this affect the perception of Islamic thought?
Denying Islamic methodology undermines the originality and authority of Islamic sciences.
4
Appreciate the book's role
How does this foreword frame the importance of the book? The book is presented as a response to these currents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ، والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وأصحابه أجمعين ، وبعد . . فهذه هي الطبعة الثالثة من هذا الكتاب الممتاز تظهر بعد أن انتقل صاحبه إلى جوار ربه . ولست في حاجة إلى الاشارة الى أهمية الكتاب ولا إلى قيمته العلمية ، فذلك أمر مشهور مؤكد لدى أهل الاختصاص . على أني أود أن ألفت إلى غاية مهمة من غايات هذا الكتاب ، ومن غايات أستاذنا النشار في الوقت نفسه ، فقد كان رحمه الله طاقة فكرية متوهجة لا تكاد تهدأ ، وقد ظل يسعى جاهداً ونحن نتلمذ له أوائل الخمسينيات أن يغرس فينا الوعي « بالمنهج » ؛ فقد كانت هذه القضية شغله الشاغل ، بل لعلها كانت هدفه الوحيد ؛ ذلك أن الناس كانت تتوزعهم تيارات متعارضة تعارضاً عنيفاً في ذلك الوقت ؛ وكان الصوت العالي حينذاك لهذا التيار الذي لم يكن يرى للمسلمين منهجاً متميزاً في ذاته ، وأن المنهج الذي ينتمون إليه هو المنهج اليوناني وبخاصة منهج أرسطو ، ومن ثم كانوا يرون في ابن رشد والفارابي وابن سينا الصورة الحقيقية للفكر الإسلامي ، ولا شك أن هذا التيار كان يلقى دعماً من دوائر الفكر الغربية لما يؤكده من أصالة الفكر اليوناني الغربي واعتماد المسلمين عليه . يضاف إلى ذلك تيار آخر غير بعيد من هذا ، يوائم بين الفكر الإسلامي وجذور البيئات المختلفة التي انتقل إليها من هندية وفارسية وفرعونية
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, and may peace and blessings be upon our master Muhammad and upon his family and companions altogether, and after... This is the third edition of this excellent book appearing after its owner passed away. I am not in need to point to the importance of the book nor its scientific value, for that is a well-known confirmed matter among specialists. However, I wish to draw attention to an important goal of this book, and also the goals of our professor al-Nashshar at the same time. He, may Allah have mercy on him, was an intellectually glowing energy that hardly calmed, and he continued striving while we were his students in the early fifties to instill in us awareness of 'methodology'; for this issue was his main preoccupation, perhaps his only goal. That is because at that time people were divided by conflicting currents in violent opposition; and the loud voice then was for this current which did not see that Muslims have a distinctive methodology in itself, and that the methodology they belong to is the Greek methodology, especially Aristotle's methodology, and thus they saw in Ibn Rushd, al-Farabi, and Ibn Sina the true image of Islamic thought. Undoubtedly, this current received support from Western intellectual circles because it confirmed the originality of Western Greek thought and Muslims' dependence upon it. Added to this is another current not far from this, reconciling Islamic thought with the roots of the various environments it moved into, from Indian, Persian, and Pharaonic.
Source pages p. 2

Commentary
This passage is a foreword to the third edition of the book. It begins with the basmalah and salutation. The writer notes that this edition appears after the author's death. He asserts the book's well-known importance. He then draws attention to a major goal of the book: the author, Dr. al-Nashshar, tirelessly worked to instill awareness of 'methodology' (al-manhaj) in his students. This was his primary concern, perhaps his sole objective. The writer explains that at the time, people were split by conflicting currents. The dominant current denied that Muslims had a distinctive methodology, claiming their methodology was essentially Greek (especially Aristotelian), and pointed to Ibn Rushd, al-Farabi, and Ibn Sina as representative. This current received Western backing because it affirmed the originality of Greek thought and Muslim dependence on it. Another current, not far from this, sought to reconcile Islamic thought with influences from Indian, Persian, and Pharaonic cultures. Thus, the author's work aimed to counter these trends by establishing a uniquely Islamic methodology.

Key Terms
المنهج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the foreword, what was the main goal that the author aimed to instill in his students?
A) Memorization of Aristotle's works
B) Awareness of the Islamic methodology (al-manhaj)
C) Following the Greek philosophers
D) Reconciling Islamic thought with Persian philosophy

Key Takeaway
The author's mission was to instill awareness of a distinct Islamic methodology, countering currents that denied it or blended it with foreign elements.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Read a passage from al-Shafi'i's al-Risala on the methodology of deriving rulings. Identify how he establishes a uniquely Islamic method.
?
2. Compare the approach of a mutakallim and a faqih in defining the sources of knowledge. Which elements reflect an Islamic methodology?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Indigenous Islamic Methodology: Usul al-Fiqh and Kalam
Editor introduces the book's methodological stance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two indigenous sources of Islamic methodology according to al-Nashshar (usul al-fiqh and ilm al-kalam) and contrast them with the Greek methodology advocated by opposing currents.

Core Idea
True Islamic methodology is indigenous, rooted in usul al-fiqh and kalam, not borrowed from Greece.

This preface sets the stage for the entire book by revealing the intellectual battle over the origins of Islamic methodology. The editor, Dr. Abduh al-Rajihi, summarizes the author al-Nashshar's lifelong mission: to prove that Muslims possess a distinctive method of reasoning found in their own sciences, not in Aristotle. Understanding this context is essential before diving into the logical tools the book teaches.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central problem
The preface describes two opposing intellectual currents in the early 1950s. The first claimed Muslims have no original methodology but rely on Greek (Aristotelian) logic. The second harmonized Islamic thought with pre-Islamic roots. Read the opening paragraphs to identify these currents.
Look for phrases like 'لا يرى للمسلمين منهجاً متميزاً' and 'يوائم بين الفكر الإسلامي وجذور البيئات المختلفة'.
2
Extract the author's thesis
Al-Nashshar, following his teacher Mustafa Abd al-Raziq, opposed both currents. He argued that the true Islamic methodology lies in two indigenous sciences. Find the sentence that names these sciences. What are they?
The key phrase: 'المنهج الإسلامي الحق ينبغي تلمسه في علمين أصيلين هما: علم أصول الفقه، وعلم الكلام'.
3
Understand how al-Nashshar developed this
The preface explains that while al-Nashshar took the idea from his teacher, he transformed it into a coherent theory because of his deep knowledge of Greek philosophy and Western methods. How did this help him?
He could engage with Greek thought from the inside and then show the superiority of Islamic methodology.
4
Connect to the book's purpose
The preface states that this book directed many researchers to study Islamic thought 'within the general framework of the methodology of the people of usul and theologians'. This is the key takeaway: the book is not just about formal logic, but about an Islamic approach to reasoning rooted in usul al-fiqh and kalam.
This frames why the tools taught in the book are distinctively Islamic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ، والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وأصحابه أجمعين ، وبعد . . فهذه هي الطبعة الثالثة من هذا الكتاب الممتاز تظهر بعد أن انتقل صاحبه إلى جوار ربه . ولست في حاجة إلى الاشارة الى أهمية الكتاب ولا إلى قيمته العلمية ، فذلك أمر مشهور مؤكد لدى أهل الاختصاص . على أني أود أن ألفت إلى غاية مهمة من غايات هذا الكتاب ، ومن غايات أستاذنا النشار في الوقت نفسه ، فقد كان رحمه الله طاقة فكرية متوهجة لا تكاد تهدأ ، وقد ظل يسعى جاهداً ونحن نتلمذ له أوائل الخمسينيات أن يغرس فينا الوعي « بالمنهج » ؛ فقد كانت هذه القضية شغله الشاغل ، بل لعلها كانت هدفه الوحيد ؛ ذلك أن الناس كانت تتوزعهم تيارات متعارضة تعارضاً عنيفاً في ذلك الوقت ؛ وكان الصوت العالي حينذاك لهذا التيار الذي لم يكن يرى للمسلمين منهجاً متميزاً في ذاته ، وأن المنهج الذي ينتمون إليه هو المنهج اليوناني وبخاصة منهج أرسطو ، ومن ثم كانوا يرون في ابن رشد والفارابي وابن سينا الصورة الحقيقية للفكر الإسلامي ، ولا شك أن هذا التيار كان يلقى دعماً من دوائر الفكر الغربية لما يؤكده من أصالة الفكر اليوناني الغربي واعتماد المسلمين عليه . يضاف إلى ذلك تيار آخر غير بعيد من هذا ، يوائم بين الفكر الإسلامي وجذور البيئات المختلفة التي انتقل إليها من هندية وفارسية وفرعونية وغيرها ، ولقد رأينا تطبيقات كثيرة لأصحاب هذا الاتجاه في تفسير النشاط الفعلي عند المسلمين . وكان أستاذنا النشار قد تلمذ للشيخ مصطفى عبد الرازق الذي كان يبشر بالاتجاه المخالف ، وهو الذي يرى أن « المنهج » الإسلامي الحق ينبغي تلمسه في علمين أصيلين هما : علم أصول الفقه ، وعلم الكلام . وقد أخذ أستاذنا النشار عنه هذا الاتجاه ، لكنه هو الذي طوره وجعله نظرية متماسكة بما توافر لديه من أدوات لم تكن متاحة لاستاده الشيخ ؛ ذلك أن النشار قد اتصل بالفكر اليوناني اتصالا وثيقاً ، واتصل بمناهج الفلسفة الغربية في لغاتها ، ومن ثم استطاع أن يفهم هذه الاشياء من داخلها . وقد كان هذا الكتاب أول ما كتب النشار ، وظل واحداً من أهم أعماله الكثيرة التي قدمها ، كما أن أهميته ترجع إلى أنه استطاع أن يوجه تفكير عدد من الباحثين في جيلنا ، ومنهم صاحب هذه السطور ، الى دراسة الفكر الإسلامي في إطار المنهج العام لأصحاب الأصول ولعلماء الكلام ، وقد ظهر عدد لا بأس به من الدراسات في اللغة والأدب والبلاغة والفلسفة يحمل هذا الطابع . وحين نفدت طبعات هذا الكتاب ، رأينا ألا نحرم الأجيال التاليه من هذا الفكر العظيم ، وقد حملت دار النهضة العربية مشكورة هذه الامانة . رحم الله أستاذنا الجليل ، وجزاه عنا خير الجزاء . الاسكندرية في ٨ من رمضان ١٤٠٤هـ ٨ من حزيران (يونية) ١٩٨٤م الدكتور عبده الراجحي أستاذ العلوم اللغوية كلية الآداب - جامعة الإسكندرية
In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, and blessings and peace be upon our master Muhammad and upon his family and all his companions. To proceed: This is the third edition of this distinguished book, appearing after its author passed to the mercy of his Lord. I do not need to point out the importance of the book nor its scholarly value, for that is a well-known and confirmed matter among specialists. However, I would like to draw attention to an important aim of this book, and also of our teacher al-Nashshar at the same time. For he, may God have mercy on him, was a glowing intellectual energy that hardly rested, and he strove earnestly while we were his students in the early fifties to instill in us awareness of 'methodology'; for this issue was his primary concern, indeed perhaps his only goal. This is because people at that time were distributed among violently conflicting currents. The loud voice then belonged to that current which did not see that Muslims had a distinctive methodology in itself, and that the methodology they belong to is the Greek methodology, especially the methodology of Aristotle. Hence they saw in Ibn Rushd, al-Farabi, and Ibn Sina the true picture of Islamic thought. Undoubtedly this current received support from Western intellectual circles because it confirmed the originality of Western Greek thought and the Muslims' dependence upon it. Added to that is another current not far from this, which harmonizes Islamic thought with the roots of the various environments into which it moved: Indian, Persian, Pharaonic and others. We have seen many applications of the proponents of this direction in interpreting the actual activity among Muslims. Our teacher al-Nashshar had studied under Shaykh Mustafa Abd al-Raziq, who preached the opposite direction, and who believed that the true Islamic 'methodology' should be perceived in two original sciences: usul al-fiqh and ilm al-kalam. Our teacher al-Nashshar took this direction from him, but he it was who developed it and made it a coherent theory with the tools available to him that were not available to his teacher. This is because al-Nashshar had close contact with Greek thought, and connected with Western philosophical methodologies in their languages, and thus he was able to understand these things from within. This book was the first that al-Nashshar wrote, and it remained one of the most important of his many works. Its importance also lies in the fact that it was able to direct the thinking of a number of researchers in our generation, including the writer of these lines, toward studying Islamic thought within the general framework of the methodology of the people of usul and theologians. A considerable number of studies in language, literature, rhetoric, and philosophy have appeared carrying this character. When the editions of this book were exhausted, we decided not to deprive the following generations of this great thought. The Dar al-Nahda al-Arabiya, may it be thanked, undertook this trust. May God have mercy on our esteemed teacher, and reward him well. Alexandria, 8 Ramadan 1404 AH, 8 June 1984 CE. Dr. Abduh al-Rajihi, Professor of Linguistic Sciences, Faculty of Arts, Alexandria University.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is a preface written by Dr. Abduh al-Rajihi for the third edition of 'Manahij Bahth'. It serves to introduce the book and highlight its central theme: the issue of methodology (al-manhaj) in Islamic thought. The editor praises the book's author, al-Nashshar, describing him as a tireless intellectual who sought to instill awareness of methodology in his students during the early 1950s. The passage then outlines two opposing intellectual currents prevalent at the time. The first current, which was dominant, held that Muslims did not possess a distinctive methodology; rather, their methodology was Greek, especially Aristotelian, as seen in figures like Ibn Rushd, al-Farabi, and Ibn Sina. This view was reinforced by Western intellectual circles. The second current, which was similar, attempted to harmonize Islamic thought with pre-Islamic roots such as Indian, Persian, and Pharaonic ideas. In contrast, al-Nashshar's teacher, Shaykh Mustafa Abd al-Raziq, advocated a different direction, asserting that true Islamic methodology should be found in two indigenous sciences: usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence) and ilm al-kalam (theology). Al-Nashshar adopted this view and, through his deep engagement with Greek thought and Western philosophical methods, developed it into a comprehensive theory. The book is thus positioned as a foundational work that directed many researchers, including the editor, to study Islamic thought within the framework of usul and kalam. The preface concludes with a note about the republication and a prayer for the author.

Key Terms
المنهج
أصول الفقه
علم الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preface, what two sciences did Shaykh Mustafa Abd al-Raziq identify as the source of true Islamic methodology?
A) Greek philosophy and Aristotelian logic
B) Usul al-fiqh and ilm al-kalam
C) Indian and Persian thought
D) Ibn Rushd and Ibn Sina's works

Key Takeaway
Al-Nashshar's book defends the thesis that Islamic methodology is indigenous, found in usul al-fiqh and kalam, not borrowed from Greek sources.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify the two main intellectual currents described in the preface and write a short paragraph contrasting them. Then explain how al-Nashshar's position differs from both.
?
Search for a short passage from usul al-fiqh (e.g., from al-Shafi‘i's al-Risala) that exemplifies the method of reasoning by analogy (qiyas). Compare it to a simple Aristotelian categorical syllogism. How are they similar? How do they differ in terms of premises and purpose?

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
The Authentic Islamic Method: Usul al-Fiqh and Kalam
A student describes the teacher's approach emphasizing usul al-fiqh and kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the authentic Islamic methodology (usul al-fiqh and kalam) from Greek logic and explain why this distinction matters for studying Islamic thought.

Core Idea
The true Islamic method is found in usul al-fiqh and kalam, not Greek logic.

This passage from the foreword of the book explains the intellectual lineage of the author and his teacher. It presents a crucial claim: the authentic Islamic methodology is not Greek logic but two indigenous sciences. Understanding this distinction changes how we approach Islamic philosophy and theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim about Islamic methodology
The teacher (Mustafa Abd al-Raziq) asserts that the true Islamic method is found in two specific sciences. Which are they?
Look for the terms 'usul al-fiqh' and 'kalam' in the passage.
2
Trace the intellectual lineage
The author al-Nashshar took this from his teacher but developed it further. Why could he develop it? Because he had direct access to Greek and Western sources, allowing him to understand these methods from within.
Contrast the teacher's and student's levels of engagement with non-Islamic thought.
3
Evaluate the significance of the claim
This claim challenges the dominance of Greek logic in Islamic studies. Why does it matter for researchers? It suggests that Islamic thought has its own rigorous methodology.
Consider how this affects the study of Islamic philosophy today.
4
Connect to the book's purpose
The passage says this book directed researchers to study Islamic thought within the framework of usul and kalam. How does this lesson guide your own reading of the book?
Think about what methodological lens you will apply as you read.

وغيرها ، ولقد رأينا تطبيقات كثيرة لأصحاب هذا الاتجاه في تفسير النشاط الفعلي عند المسلمين . وكان أستاذنا النشار قد تلمذ للشيخ مصطفى عبد الرازق الذي كان يبشر بالاتجاه المخالف ، وهو الذي يرى أن « المنهج » الإسلامي الحق ينبغي تلمسه في علمين أصيلين هما : علم أصول الفقه ، وعلم الكلام . وقد أخذ أستاذنا النشار عنه هذا الاتجاه ، لكنه هو الذي طوره وجعله نظرية متماسكة بما توافر لديه من أدوات لم تكن متاحة لاستاده الشيخ ؛ ذلك أن النشار قد اتصل بالفكر اليوناني اتصالا وثيقاً ، واتصل بمناهج الفلسفة الغربية في لغاتها ، ومن ثم استطاع أن يفهم هذه الاشياء من داخلها . وقد كان هذا الكتاب أول ما كتب النشار ، وظل واحداً من أهم أعماله الكثيرة التي قدمها ، كما أن أهميته ترجع إلى أنه استطاع أن يوجه تفكير عدد من الباحثين في جيلنا ، ومنهم صاحب هذه السطور ، الى دراسة الفكر الإسلامي في إطار المنهج العام لأصحاب الأصول ولعلماء الكلام ، وقد ظهر عدد لا بأس به من الدراسات في اللغة والأدب والبلاغة والفلسفة يحمل هذا الطابع . وحين نفدت طبعات هذا الكتاب ، رأينا ألا نحرم الأجيال التاليه من هذا الفكر العظيم ، وقد حملت دار النهضة العربية مشكورة هذه الامانة . رحم الله أستاذنا الجليل ، وجزاه عنا خير الجزاء . الاسكندرية في ٨ من رمضان ١٤٠٤هـ ٨ من حزيران (يونية) ١٩٨٤م الدكتور عبده الراجحي أستاذ العلوم اللغوية كلية الآداب - جامعة الإسكندرية
And others. We have seen many applications by the proponents of this direction in interpreting the practical activity of Muslims. Our teacher al-Nashshar was a student of Sheikh Mustafa Abd al-Raziq, who heralded the opposite direction, who holds that the true Islamic 'method' should be sought in two authentic sciences: usul al-fiqh and kalam. Our teacher al-Nashshar took this direction from him, but he developed it and made it a coherent theory using tools that were not available to his teacher. This is because al-Nashshar had thorough contact with Greek thought and with Western philosophical methodologies in their languages, and thus was able to understand these things from within. This book was al-Nashshar's first work and remained one of his most important contributions. Its importance also lies in the fact that it directed the thinking of many researchers of our generation, including the writer of these lines, to the study of Islamic thought within the general framework of the method of the usul scholars and theologians. A considerable number of studies in language, literature, rhetoric, and philosophy have appeared bearing this character. When this book's editions went out of print, we decided not to deprive later generations of this great thought. The Arab Renaissance Publishing House, may it be thanked, undertook this trust. May God have mercy on our great teacher and reward him well. Alexandria, 8 Ramadan 1404 AH / 8 June 1984 AD. Dr. Abduh al-Rajihi, Professor of Linguistic Sciences, Faculty of Arts - University of Alexandria.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note by Dr. Abduh al-Rajihi, a student of the author, explaining the intellectual lineage and methodological orientation of the author. It opens by referencing a prior discussion about applications of a certain approach. It then highlights that the teacher, al-Nashshar, was a student of Sheikh Mustafa Abd al-Raziq, who championed the view that the true Islamic methodology is to be found not in Greek logic but in two indigenous sciences: usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence) and kalam (scholastic theology). Al-Nashshar took this direction but developed it into a coherent theory thanks to his deep engagement with Greek thought and Western philosophy. The passage emphasizes that this book was al-Nashshar's first and that it successfully directed researchers, including the commentator himself, to study Islamic thought within the framework of usul and kalam. It concludes with a note on the republication and a prayer for the teacher.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه
علم الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, where should the true Islamic methodology be sought?
A) In Greek philosophy and logic
B) In usul al-fiqh and kalam
C) In Western scientific methods
D) In the practices of the early caliphs

Key Takeaway
The passage asserts that the true Islamic method lies in usul al-fiqh and kalam, not in Greek logic, and that the author's work embodies this approach.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a passage in a work of Islamic theology (e.g., al-Sanusiyya) and compare its reasoning method to the method described in the passage. Does it rely more on usul/kalam categories or on Greek logic? Provide a brief analysis.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Author's Aim: Presenting Authentic Islamic Thought vs. Orientalist Claims
Author states the goal of presenting the authentic Islamic model and refutes Orientalist claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's stated purpose in writing the book and the Orientalist claim he refutes regarding Islamic methodology.

Core Idea
Islamic thought is not a copy of Greek civilization but an independent model flowing from the Qur'an and Sunnah.

In this preface to the second edition, the author declares his mission: to present the supreme model of Islamic thought. He directly confronts the Orientalist narrative that Islamic civilization merely borrowed from Greek thought and that Muslims had no methodology beyond Aristotelian logic. This sets the stage for the entire book, which aims to articulate the authentic Islamic methodological framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's goal
Read the first sentence. The author says his aim was to present the supreme model of Islamic thought, which expresses the spirit of Islamic civilization and flows from the Quran and Sunnah.
This goal is explicitly stated.
2
Extract the Orientalist claim
Find the part where the author reports what Europe and its scholars claimed: that Muslims adopted Greek philosophy and that Islamic civilization is a distorted copy of Greek civilization.
The author is summarizing the opposing view to refute it.

The author says the weapon used to dominate the 'Greek temptation' was research into methodology. Orientalists and missionaries claimed Muslims only embraced Aristotelian logic and had no other methodology.

By presenting his book, the author implicitly argues that Islamic thought has its own authentic methodology, independent of Greek logic. The entire book is meant to articulate this.
This frames the rest of the work.

تَصْدِيرُ الطَّبْعَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ كانت غايتي من كتابة هذا الكتاب أن أقدم نموذج الفكر الإسلامي الأعلى ، النموذج الوحيد المعبر عن روح الحضارة الإسلامية ، والمنبعث في تدفق سيال من روح القرآن وسنة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم . حاولت أوروبا - أو العالم الغربي - خلال علمائها ومفكريها أن تفرض علينا « ثقافة » أوروبا « وحضارتها » مدعية أن أسلافنا - من قبل - فعلوا هذا حين أخذوا بفلسفة اليونان وحضارة اليونان . وقالوا إن الحضارة الإسلامية لم تكن سوى صورة مشوهة لحضارة اليونان أو لم تكن غير جسر عبرت عليه هذه الحضارة إلى أوروبا . كانت حضارة الإسلام إذن وفكر الإسلام إذن - في رأي هؤلاء - ذيلاً لحضارة اليونان ، وترديداً لها . وقد تابع أوروبا في العقود الأربعة الأولى من هذا القرن - هذا الجيل المأفون ، ممن دعوا بالمجددين وقادة الفكر . ورجال الرأي . . . وكان سلاح هؤلاء جميعاً العلمي في سيطرة الفتنة اليونانية ، البحث في المنهج واندفع هؤلاء المستشرقون والمبشرون وأذنابهم يعلنون أن المسلمين احتضنوا منهج الحضارة اليونانية ، المنطق الارسططاليسي ، وأنه لم يكن لهم ثمة منهج غيره . وقد كان المنطق الارسططاليسي ، وسم الحضارة اليونانية ، والفكر اليوناني ، والمعبر النهائي عن جوهرها
Preface to the Second Edition. My aim in writing this book was to present the higher model of Islamic thought, the only model that expresses the spirit of Islamic civilization, and which flows from the spirit of the Qur'an and the Sunnah of Muhammad (peace be upon him). Europe - or the Western world - through its scholars and thinkers, attempted to impose upon us the 'culture' of Europe and its 'civilization', claiming that our ancestors had done this before when they adopted Greek philosophy and Greek civilization. They said that Islamic civilization was nothing but a distorted image of Greek civilization, or merely a bridge over which this civilization passed to Europe. Islamic civilization and thought were therefore, in their view, a tail to Greek civilization and a repetition of it. And in the first four decades of this century, this misguided generation, who called themselves reformers and leaders of thought and opinion, followed Europe. Their scientific weapon in dominating the Greek temptation was the investigation of methodology. These Orientalists, missionaries, and their followers rushed to announce that the Muslims had embraced the methodology of Greek civilization, that is, Aristotelian logic, and that they had no other methodology besides it. And Aristotelian logic was the hallmark of Greek civilization, Greek thought, and the ultimate expression of its essence.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the preface to the second edition, in which the author sets out his purpose. He begins by stating that his goal is to present the supreme model of Islamic thought, uniquely expressive of Islamic civilization, emanating from the Qur'an and Sunnah. He then critiques the Western/European claim that Muslim ancestors merely borrowed from Greek civilization, and that Islamic civilization is only a distorted copy or a bridge for Greek ideas to reach Europe. He notes that some modernists within the Islamic world followed this European narrative. He identifies the 'scientific weapon' of this trend as the focus on methodology, specifically the assertion that Muslims adopted Aristotelian logic as their only methodology. The author implies that this is a false accusation and sets the stage for his own work to present the authentic Islamic methodological approach.

نموذج الفكر الإسلامي الأعلى

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Author's Aim and the Western Narrative
Author introduces his aim and counters Western narratives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's stated aim and contrast it with the Western narrative that Islamic civilization copied Greek thought.

Core Idea
Islamic methodology is rooted in revelation, not Greece.

In this foreword, the author immediately sets the record straight: his book aims to present the authentic Islamic model, not a derivative of Greek philosophy. He then summarizes the Western claim that Islamic civilization was merely a bridge for Greek ideas to Europe. Understanding this tension is crucial before diving into the book's logical content.

Guided Path
1
Locate the author's stated goal
Find the sentence beginning 'كانت غايتي' in the Arabic text. What does the author say he aims to present?
2
Identify the sources of the model
What does the author say is the source of the 'highest model of Islamic thought'? Look for the phrase 'المنبعث في تدفق سيال من روح القرآن وسنة محمد'
3
Summarize the Western claim
In your own words, restate what European scholars allege about Islamic civilization according to the author.
4
Analyze the author's language

تَصْدِيرُ الطَّبْعَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ
كانت غايتي من كتابة هذا الكتاب أن أقدم نموذج الفكر الإسلامي الأعلى ، النموذج الوحيد المعبر عن روح الحضارة الإسلامية ، والمنبعث في تدفق سيال من روح القرآن وسنة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم .
حاولت أوروبا - أو العالم الغربي - خلال علمائها ومفكريها أن تفرض علينا « ثقافة » أوروبا « وحضارتها » مدعية أن أسلافنا - من قبل - فعلوا هذا حين أخذوا بفلسفة اليونان وحضارة اليونان . وقالوا إن الحضارة الإسلامية لم تكن سوى صورة مشوهة لحضارة اليونان أو لم تكن غير جسر عبرت عليه هذه الحضارة إلى أوروبا . كانت حضارة الإسلام إذن وفكر الإسلام إذن - في رأي هؤلاء - ذيلاً لحضارة اليونان ، وترديداً لها . وقد تابع أوروبا في العقود الأربعة الأولى من هذا القرن - هذا الجيل المأفون ، ممن دعوا بالمجددين وقادة الفكر . ورجال الرأي . . .
وكان سلاح هؤلاء جميعاً العلمي في سيطرة الفتنة اليونانية ، البحث في المنهج واندفع هؤلاء المستشرقون والمبشرون وأذنابهم يعلنون أن المسلمين احتضنوا منهج الحضارة اليونانية ، المنطق الارسططاليسي ، وأنه لم يكن لهم ثمة منهج غيره . وقد كان المنطق الارسططاليسي ، وسم الحضارة اليونانية ، والفكر اليوناني ، والمعبر النهائي عن جوهرها .

وأنا أعلم أن « روزبه » القديم - عبد الله بن المقفع - وكان أكبر ضاغن على الإسلام في القديم ، قدم أول ما قدم للقضاء على نظام الإسلام الاجتماعي - كتاب مزدك ، ثم كتب باب برزويه ليثبت تناقض الأديان - وبخاصة الإسلام - وعدم يقينيتها وما يظهر له فيها من تناقض بينما يؤكد يقينية الفلسفة ووصولها الى الحق المطلق . ثم قدم أو دفع ابنه محمد بن عبد الله بن المقفع ليقدم أول ترجمة لعلم ظن أنه الصورة الكبرى لليقين قانون بديهي في نظره ، في أفق فوق الخطأ . فاذا أعلن المسلمون أن كتابهم المقدس لا يأتيه الباطل من بين يديه ولا من خلفه ، أشار لهم إلى باب برزويه ، الذي يقرر خطأ الكتاب وتناقضه ، وأن طريق الفلسفة هو صورة طريق اليقين ، ثم يدعم كل هذا بصور من المنطق الارسططاليسي ، البناء المتكامل اليقيني في نظره . .
لقد غرس روزبه الغرس ، وأتى ثمره ، فنشأت مجامع الغنوصية الخطيرة في إثر روزبه ، كما تناول المنطق ، متفلسفة ظهروا في الإسلام ، ومجدوه ، ورفعوه فوق كل يقين . وحاولوا مزجه بكل علم إسلامي .
ولم تكن الجماعة الإسلامية غافلة عن كل هذا . فسرعان ما تناولت هذا المنطق الارسططاليسي بالدراسة والتمحيص فمزقته كل ممزق وأنشأت منهجها .
بل كان المنهج - قد تكون منذ البدء - مستنداً على القرآن والسنة ، معبراً عن روح الإسلام الحقيقي إن البعث الحقيقي للروح الإسلامية وللأمة الإسلامية هو العودة الكاملة لهذا المنهج ، هو الأخذ بنصوص القرآن والسنة والعودة الى قانونهما .
ان خلفاء روزبه كثيرون في عصرنا ، وقد تعددت أشكالهم ، وتنوعت صورهم ، ولكن هم جميعاً نسخ مشوهة منتنة لابن المقفع الكريه . ولقد فشل ابن المقفع من قبل ، وهم أيضاً فاشلون .
Foreword of the Second Edition
My goal in writing this book was to present the highest model of Islamic thought, the only model expressing the spirit of Islamic civilization, emanating in a flowing stream from the spirit of the Qur'an and the Sunnah of Muhammad, peace be upon him.
Europe - or the Western world - through its scholars and thinkers, tried to impose upon us the 'culture' of Europe and its 'civilization', claiming that our predecessors did this before when they adopted Greek philosophy and Greek civilization. They said that Islamic civilization was only a distorted image of Greek civilization, or was nothing but a bridge upon which this civilization crossed to Europe. Thus, in their view, Islamic civilization and Islamic thought were a tail to Greek civilization, an echo of it. In the first four decades of this century, this corrupted generation followed Europe, those who called themselves reformers and leaders of thought and men of opinion.
The scientific weapon of all of them in mastering the Greek temptation was the study of methodology. These orientalists, missionaries, and their henchmen rushed to announce that the Muslims embraced the methodology of Greek civilization, Aristotelian logic, and that they had no other methodology. Aristotelian logic was the brand of Greek civilization, Greek thought, and the ultimate expression of its essence.
And I know that the ancient 'Ruzbeh' - Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' - was the greatest enemy of Islam in ancient times. He first presented to destroy the social system of Islam - the book of Mazdak, then wrote the chapters of Barzawayh to prove the contradiction of religions - especially Islam - and their lack of certainty, and what appears to him of contradiction in them, while affirming the certainty of philosophy and its attainment of absolute truth. Then he presented or pushed his son Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' to present the first translation of a science that he thought was the great form of certainty, a self-evident law in his view, above error. So when the Muslims declared that their sacred book is not approached by falsehood from before it or from behind it, he pointed them to the chapters of Barzawayh, which establishes the book's error and contradiction, and that the path of philosophy is the path of certainty, then he supports all this with images of Aristotelian logic, the integrated certain edifice in his view.
Ruzbeh planted the seed, and it bore fruit. Dangerous gnostic gatherings arose after Ruzbeh, and they took up logic. Philosophers appeared in Islam, glorified it, and elevated it above all certainty. They tried to mix it with every Islamic science.
The Islamic community was not unaware of all this. Soon they took up this Aristotelian logic with study and scrutiny, tearing it apart completely, and established their own methodology.
Rather, the methodology - perhaps constituted from the beginning - was based on the Qur'an and Sunnah, expressing the true spirit of Islam. The real revival of the Islamic spirit and the Islamic nation is the complete return to this methodology, taking the texts of the Qur'an and Sunnah and returning to their laws.
The successors of Ruzbeh are many in our time; their forms have multiplied and their images varied, but they are all distorted, foul copies of the repulsive Ibn al-Muqaffa'. Ibn al-Muqaffa' failed before, and they too are failures.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the foreword to the second edition of the book 'Manahij Bahth'. The author opens by stating his goal: to present the highest model of Islamic thought that expresses the spirit of Islamic civilization, which flows from the Qur'an and Sunnah. He then critiques Western scholars who claim that Islamic civilization merely copied Greek philosophy and that Aristotelian logic was the only method used by Muslims. The author argues that this is a distortion. He then brings a historical account of Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' (known as Ruzbeh), an early adversary of Islam, who translated Greek logic and used it to attack the certainty of divine revelation. The author describes how Ibn al-Muqaffa' presented the 'Book of Mazdak' and the 'Chapters of Barzawayh' to undermine Islam, and how his son translated Aristotelian logic. The author asserts that Muslim scholars later examined Aristotelian logic and refuted it, establishing their own methodology based directly on the Qur'an and Sunnah. He concludes by warning against modern successors of Ibn al-Muqaffa' who continue to spread foreign methodologies, and emphasizes that the true revival of the Islamic nation lies in returning to the original Islamic methodology derived from revelation.

Key Terms
المنطق الارسططاليسي
اليقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the foundation of Islamic thought and methodology?
A) Greek philosophy adopted by early Muslims
B) The Qur'an and Sunnah of Muhammad
C) Aristotelian logic as translated by Ibn al-Muqaffa'
D) The mystical traditions of gnosticism

Key Takeaway
Islamic methodology is not borrowed from Greece but is derived directly from revelation.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Ibn al-Muqaffa' and the Introduction of Aristotelian Logic
Author recounts the historical introduction of Greek logic by an adversary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Ibn al-Muqaffa' used Aristotelian logic to undermine the certainty of revelation, according to the author.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Muqaffa' weaponized logic to attack Islam's claim to certainty.

The author singles out Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' as the ancient enemy who first brought Aristotelian logic into the Islamic world as a tool to challenge the Qur'an's inerrancy. He describes how Ibn al-Muqaffa' used translations and writings to promote philosophy over revelation. This historical account illustrates the author's view that logic was not a neutral tool but a weapon in an ideological war.

Guided Path
1
Identify the figure Ruzbeh
Find the name 'روزبه' in the Arabic text. Who is he and what is his role according to the author?
2
List the works he introduced
What are the two works mentioned (كتاب مزدك and باب برزويه) and what was their purpose?
3
Explain how he used logic
How did Ibn al-Muqaffa' use Aristotelian logic to argue against the certainty of revelation? Look for the contrast between 'اليقين' of philosophy and the 'تناقض' of religions.
4
Reflect on the author's characterization
Why does the author call Ibn al-Muqaffa' the 'greatest enemy of Islam'? What makes his actions particularly dangerous?

Foreword of the Second Edition
My goal in writing this book was to present the highest model of Islamic thought, the only model expressing the spirit of Islamic civilization, emanating in a flowing stream from the spirit of the Qur'an and the Sunnah of Muhammad, peace be upon him.
Europe - or the Western world - through its scholars and thinkers, tried to impose upon us the 'culture' of Europe and its 'civilization', claiming that our predecessors did this before when they adopted Greek philosophy and Greek civilization. They said that Islamic civilization was only a distorted image of Greek civilization, or was nothing but a bridge upon which this civilization crossed to Europe. Thus, in their view, Islamic civilization and Islamic thought were a tail to Greek civilization, an echo of it. In the first four decades of this century, this corrupted generation followed Europe, those who called themselves reformers and leaders of thought and men of opinion.
The scientific weapon of all of them in mastering the Greek temptation was the study of methodology. These orientalists, missionaries, and their henchmen rushed to announce that the Muslims embraced the methodology of Greek civilization, Aristotelian logic, and that they had no other methodology. Aristotelian logic was the brand of Greek civilization, Greek thought, and the ultimate expression of its essence.
And I know that the ancient 'Ruzbeh' - Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' - was the greatest enemy of Islam in ancient times. He first presented to destroy the social system of Islam - the book of Mazdak, then wrote the chapters of Barzawayh to prove the contradiction of religions - especially Islam - and their lack of certainty, and what appears to him of contradiction in them, while affirming the certainty of philosophy and its attainment of absolute truth. Then he presented or pushed his son Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' to present the first translation of a science that he thought was the great form of certainty, a self-evident law in his view, above error. So when the Muslims declared that their sacred book is not approached by falsehood from before it or from behind it, he pointed them to the chapters of Barzawayh, which establishes the book's error and contradiction, and that the path of philosophy is the path of certainty, then he supports all this with images of Aristotelian logic, the integrated certain edifice in his view.
Ruzbeh planted the seed, and it bore fruit. Dangerous gnostic gatherings arose after Ruzbeh, and they took up logic. Philosophers appeared in Islam, glorified it, and elevated it above all certainty. They tried to mix it with every Islamic science.
The Islamic community was not unaware of all this. Soon they took up this Aristotelian logic with study and scrutiny, tearing it apart completely, and established their own methodology.
Rather, the methodology - perhaps constituted from the beginning - was based on the Qur'an and Sunnah, expressing the true spirit of Islam. The real revival of the Islamic spirit and the Islamic nation is the complete return to this methodology, taking the texts of the Qur'an and Sunnah and returning to their laws.
The successors of Ruzbeh are many in our time; their forms have multiplied and their images varied, but they are all distorted, foul copies of the repulsive Ibn al-Muqaffa'. Ibn al-Muqaffa' failed before, and they too are failures.

Commentary
This passage is the foreword to the second edition of the book 'Manahij Bahth'. The author opens by stating his goal: to present the highest model of Islamic thought that expresses the spirit of Islamic civilization, which flows from the Qur'an and Sunnah. He then critiques Western scholars who claim that Islamic civilization merely copied Greek philosophy and that Aristotelian logic was the only method used by Muslims. The author argues that this is a distortion. He then brings a historical account of Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' (known as Ruzbeh), an early adversary of Islam, who translated Greek logic and used it to attack the certainty of divine revelation. The author describes how Ibn al-Muqaffa' presented the 'Book of Mazdak' and the 'Chapters of Barzawayh' to undermine Islam, and how his son translated Aristotelian logic. The author asserts that Muslim scholars later examined Aristotelian logic and refuted it, establishing their own methodology based directly on the Qur'an and Sunnah. He concludes by warning against modern successors of Ibn al-Muqaffa' who continue to spread foreign methodologies, and emphasizes that the true revival of the Islamic nation lies in returning to the original Islamic methodology derived from revelation.

Key Terms
روزبه
اليقين
المنطق الارسططاليسي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the purpose of Ibn al-Muqaffa's translation of Aristotelian logic, according to the author?
A) To help Muslims understand philosophy better
B) To prove that Islam is the true religion
C) To attack the certainty of revelation and promote philosophy
D) To establish a new school of Islamic jurisprudence

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Muqaffa' introduced Aristotelian logic as a rival to revelation, claiming it provided absolute certainty.

?

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

The Islamic Response and the True Methodology
Author describes the Islamic refutation of Greek logic and the true methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe how Muslim scholars refuted Aristotelian logic and established their own methodology based on Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Muslim scholars tore apart Aristotelian logic and built a methodology from revelation.

The author concludes the foreword by celebrating the Islamic community's response: they examined Aristotelian logic and completely refuted it, establishing a methodology rooted in the Qur'an and Sunnah. He warns against modern-day successors of Ibn al-Muqaffa' who continue to promote foreign methodologies. This lesson highlights the constructive aspect of the author's critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Islamic community's action
Find the sentence beginning 'ولم تكن الجماعة الإسلامية غافلة'. What did they do with Aristotelian logic?
2
Describe the alternative methodology
According to the author, what is the true basis of Islamic methodology? Look for 'بل كان المنهج - قد تكون منذ البدء - مستنداً على القرآن والسنة'.
3
Note the author's call for revival
What does the author say is needed for the revival of the Islamic spirit and nation?
4
Compare modern successors
Who are the modern 'successors of Ruzbeh' and why does the author compare them to Ibn al-Muqaffa'?

تَصْدِيرُ الطَّبْعَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ
كانت غايتي من كتابة هذا الكتاب أن أقدم نموذج الفكر الإسلامي الأعلى ، النموذج الوحيد المعبر عن روح الحضارة الإسلامية ، والمنبعث في تدفق سيال من روح القرآن وسنة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم .
حاولت أوروبا - أو العالم الغربي - خلال علمائها ومفكريها أن تفرض علينا « ثقافة » أوروبا « وحضارتها » مدعية أن أسلافنا - من قبل - فعلوا هذا حين أخذوا بفلسفة اليونان وحضارة اليونان . وقالوا إن الحضارة الإسلامية لم تكن سوى صورة مشوهة لحضارة اليونان أو لم تكن غير جسر عبرت عليه هذه الحضارة إلى أوروبا . كانت حضارة الإسلام إذن وفكر الإسلام إذن - في رأي هؤلاء - ذيلاً لحضارة اليونان ، وترديداً لها . وقد تابع أوروبا في العقود الأربعة الأولى من هذا القرن - هذا الجيل المأفون ، ممن دعوا بالمجددين وقادة الفكر . ورجال الرأي . . .
وكان سلاح هؤلاء جميعاً العلمي في سيطرة الفتنة اليونانية ، البحث في المنهج واندفع هؤلاء المستشرقون والمبشرون وأذنابهم يعلنون أن المسلمين احتضنوا منهج الحضارة اليونانية ، المنطق الارسططاليسي ، وأنه لم يكن لهم ثمة منهج غيره . وقد كان المنطق الارسططاليسي ، وسم الحضارة اليونانية ، والفكر اليوناني ، والمعبر النهائي عن جوهرها .

وأنا أعلم أن « روزبه » القديم - عبد الله بن المقفع - وكان أكبر ضاغن على الإسلام في القديم ، قدم أول ما قدم للقضاء على نظام الإسلام الاجتماعي - كتاب مزدك ، ثم كتب باب برزويه ليثبت تناقض الأديان - وبخاصة الإسلام - وعدم يقينيتها وما يظهر له فيها من تناقض بينما يؤكد يقينية الفلسفة ووصولها الى الحق المطلق . ثم قدم أو دفع ابنه محمد بن عبد الله بن المقفع ليقدم أول ترجمة لعلم ظن أنه الصورة الكبرى لليقين قانون بديهي في نظره ، في أفق فوق الخطأ . فاذا أعلن المسلمون أن كتابهم المقدس لا يأتيه الباطل من بين يديه ولا من خلفه ، أشار لهم إلى باب برزويه ، الذي يقرر خطأ الكتاب وتناقضه ، وأن طريق الفلسفة هو صورة طريق اليقين ، ثم يدعم كل هذا بصور من المنطق الارسططاليسي ، البناء المتكامل اليقيني في نظره . .
لقد غرس روزبه الغرس ، وأتى ثمره ، فنشأت مجامع الغنوصية الخطيرة في إثر روزبه ، كما تناول المنطق ، متفلسفة ظهروا في الإسلام ، ومجدوه ، ورفعوه فوق كل يقين . وحاولوا مزجه بكل علم إسلامي .
ولم تكن الجماعة الإسلامية غافلة عن كل هذا . فسرعان ما تناولت هذا المنطق الارسططاليسي بالدراسة والتمحيص فمزقته كل ممزق وأنشأت منهجها .
بل كان المنهج - قد تكون منذ البدء - مستنداً على القرآن والسنة ، معبراً عن روح الإسلام الحقيقي إن البعث الحقيقي للروح الإسلامية وللأمة الإسلامية هو العودة الكاملة لهذا المنهج ، هو الأخذ بنصوص القرآن والسنة والعودة الى قانونهما .
ان خلفاء روزبه كثيرون في عصرنا ، وقد تعددت أشكالهم ، وتنوعت صورهم ، ولكن هم جميعاً نسخ مشوهة منتنة لابن المقفع الكريه . ولقد فشل ابن المقفع من قبل ، وهم أيضاً فاشلون .
Foreword of the Second Edition
My goal in writing this book was to present the highest model of Islamic thought, the only model expressing the spirit of Islamic civilization, emanating in a flowing stream from the spirit of the Qur'an and the Sunnah of Muhammad, peace be upon him.
Europe - or the Western world - through its scholars and thinkers, tried to impose upon us the 'culture' of Europe and its 'civilization', claiming that our predecessors did this before when they adopted Greek philosophy and Greek civilization. They said that Islamic civilization was only a distorted image of Greek civilization, or was nothing but a bridge upon which this civilization crossed to Europe. Thus, in their view, Islamic civilization and Islamic thought were a tail to Greek civilization, an echo of it. In the first four decades of this century, this corrupted generation followed Europe, those who called themselves reformers and leaders of thought and men of opinion.
The scientific weapon of all of them in mastering the Greek temptation was the study of methodology. These orientalists, missionaries, and their henchmen rushed to announce that the Muslims embraced the methodology of Greek civilization, Aristotelian logic, and that they had no other methodology. Aristotelian logic was the brand of Greek civilization, Greek thought, and the ultimate expression of its essence.
And I know that the ancient 'Ruzbeh' - Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' - was the greatest enemy of Islam in ancient times. He first presented to destroy the social system of Islam - the book of Mazdak, then wrote the chapters of Barzawayh to prove the contradiction of religions - especially Islam - and their lack of certainty, and what appears to him of contradiction in them, while affirming the certainty of philosophy and its attainment of absolute truth. Then he presented or pushed his son Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' to present the first translation of a science that he thought was the great form of certainty, a self-evident law in his view, above error. So when the Muslims declared that their sacred book is not approached by falsehood from before it or from behind it, he pointed them to the chapters of Barzawayh, which establishes the book's error and contradiction, and that the path of philosophy is the path of certainty, then he supports all this with images of Aristotelian logic, the integrated certain edifice in his view.
Ruzbeh planted the seed, and it bore fruit. Dangerous gnostic gatherings arose after Ruzbeh, and they took up logic. Philosophers appeared in Islam, glorified it, and elevated it above all certainty. They tried to mix it with every Islamic science.
The Islamic community was not unaware of all this. Soon they took up this Aristotelian logic with study and scrutiny, tearing it apart completely, and established their own methodology.
Rather, the methodology - perhaps constituted from the beginning - was based on the Qur'an and Sunnah, expressing the true spirit of Islam. The real revival of the Islamic spirit and the Islamic nation is the complete return to this methodology, taking the texts of the Qur'an and Sunnah and returning to their laws.
The successors of Ruzbeh are many in our time; their forms have multiplied and their images varied, but they are all distorted, foul copies of the repulsive Ibn al-Muqaffa'. Ibn al-Muqaffa' failed before, and they too are failures.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the foreword to the second edition of the book 'Manahij Bahth'. The author opens by stating his goal: to present the highest model of Islamic thought that expresses the spirit of Islamic civilization, which flows from the Qur'an and Sunnah. He then critiques Western scholars who claim that Islamic civilization merely copied Greek philosophy and that Aristotelian logic was the only method used by Muslims. The author argues that this is a distortion. He then brings a historical account of Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' (known as Ruzbeh), an early adversary of Islam, who translated Greek logic and used it to attack the certainty of divine revelation. The author describes how Ibn al-Muqaffa' presented the 'Book of Mazdak' and the 'Chapters of Barzawayh' to undermine Islam, and how his son translated Aristotelian logic. The author asserts that Muslim scholars later examined Aristotelian logic and refuted it, establishing their own methodology based directly on the Qur'an and Sunnah. He concludes by warning against modern successors of Ibn al-Muqaffa' who continue to spread foreign methodologies, and emphasizes that the true revival of the Islamic nation lies in returning to the original Islamic methodology derived from revelation.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Historical Claims: Ibn al-Muqaffa' and the Introduction of Aristotelian Logic
Author introduces Ibn al-Muqaffa' as the one who introduced Aristotelian logic to challenge Islamic certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the historical narrative presented by Dr. Ali Sami al-Nashshar about the introduction of Aristotelian logic into Islam as a tool against revelation.

Core Idea
Aristotelian logic was introduced not as neutral science but as a weapon against Islamic certainty.

Dr. Nashshar opens his work by asserting that the first introduction of Aristotelian logic to the Islamic world was not a neutral transmission of knowledge. He traces it to Ibn al-Muqaffa', whom he portrays as an enemy of Islam who used logic to undermine the Quran's authority. This lesson unpacks his claim and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agent
Who does the author name as the introducer of Aristotelian logic? Look for 'عبد الله بن المقفع' and his original name 'روزبه'.
2
Identify the purpose
What was the intended purpose of introducing logic? The author claims it was to destroy the social system of Islam and to prove contradiction of scriptures.
The author links logic to the earlier work 'باب برزويه'.
3
Identify the supporting text
What text did Ibn al-Muqaffa' write to support his claims? Find 'باب برزويه'.
This text aimed to show contradictions in religions, especially Islam.
4
Identify the epistemic contrast
What did Ibn al-Muqaffa' present as the path to true certainty? The author says he presented logic as the 'supreme form of certainty' or 'self-evident law'.

٨ صفر عام ١٣٨٥هـ

And I know that the ancient 'Ruzbih' - Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' - who was the greatest resentful enemy of Islam in ancient times, first presented to destroy the social system of Islam the book of Mazdak, then wrote the chapter of Barzawayh to prove the contradiction of religions - especially Islam - and their lack of certainty, and what appears to him of contradiction, while he affirms the certainty of philosophy and its attainment of absolute truth. Then he presented or pushed his son Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' to present the first translation of a science that he thought was the supreme form of certainty, a self-evident law in his view, in a horizon above error. When Muslims declared that their holy book is not approached by falsehood from before it or from behind it, he pointed them to the chapter of Barzawayh, which asserts the error and contradiction of the book, and that the path of philosophy is the image of the path of certainty, then supports all this with forms of Aristotelian logic, the complete certain structure in his view. 
Ruzbih planted the seed and it bore fruit, so dangerous gnostic circles arose after Ruzbih, and likewise pseudo-philosophers who appeared in Islam took up logic, glorified it, and elevated it above all certainty. They tried to mix it with every Islamic science. 
And the Muslim community was not heedless of all this. Soon they took up this Aristotelian logic with study and scrutiny, tearing it apart completely and establishing their own method. 
Rather, the method - perhaps it was from the beginning - was based on the Quran and Sunnah, expressing the true spirit of Islam. The true revival of the Islamic spirit and the Islamic nation is the complete return to this method, to adhering to the texts of the Quran and Sunnah and returning to their law. 
Indeed, the successors of Ruzbih are many in our time, their forms multiplied and their images varied, but they are all distorted foul copies of the odious Ibn al-Muqaffa'. And Ibn al-Muqaffa' failed before, and they too are failures. 
The objective scientific study, which I present to all researchers in this book, definitively proves that Muslims never accepted this Aristotelian syllogistic logic; rather, they attacked and criticized it with the fiercest attack and harshest criticism. Then they developed a new logic or a new methodology - that is the inductive logic or method. And each of these methods expresses the spirit of a particular civilization, with features that differ greatly from the other. 
I wrote the first version of this book in the early years of youth (1940-1942), then published it in 1947, and now I present it in a second edition, in which the basic idea has not changed, but many additions have been made to its material, yet the book retains its original character. 
Dr. Ali Sami al-Nashshar
Professor of Islamic Philosophy
Faculty of Arts - University of Alexandria
Tuesday
8 Safar 1385 AH
8 June 1965 AD.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is the author's prefatory historical and ideological introduction. It begins by identifying Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' (originally Ruzbih) as a primary enemy of Islam who first introduced Mazdak's book to undermine Islamic social order, then wrote 'Bab Barzawayh' to claim contradictions in religions (especially Islam) while asserting philosophy's absolute certainty. He then had his son translate a work of logic, considering it the supreme form of certainty. When Muslims asserted the Quran's inerrancy, Ibn al-Muqaffa' used Bab Barzawayh to argue for the Bible's corruption and philosophy's superiority, supported by Aristotelian logic. The author then states that Ruzbih's efforts bore fruit in dangerous gnostic circles and pseudo-philosophers within Islam who glorified logic and tried to merge it with Islamic sciences. However, the Muslim community responded by scrutinizing and tearing apart Aristotelian logic, establishing their own method based on the Quran and Sunnah. The author asserts that true revival lies in returning to this method. He compares contemporary enemies to Ibn al-Muqaffa', declaring them failures. He then claims his study proves Muslims never accepted Aristotelian syllogistic logic; rather, they criticized it and developed an inductive method, each method reflecting a distinct civilizational spirit. Finally, he notes that this second edition retains the original idea with added material. The tone is polemical and patriotic, setting the stage for his own methodology.

باب برزويه

Key Takeaway
The author claims Aristotelian logic was introduced by an enemy of Islam to challenge the Quran's authority, setting the stage for a Muslim critique and alternative methodology.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Muslim Response: Rejection of Aristotelian Logic and the Inductive Method
Author describes the Muslim community's critical study of Aristotelian logic and their development of an inductive method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Muslim community's response to Aristotelian logic and the inductive methodology they developed according to Dr. Nashshar.

Core Idea
Muslims critiqued Aristotelian logic and built a distinct inductive method rooted in the Quran and Sunnah.

Dr. Nashshar emphasizes that the Muslim community was not passive. They studied Aristotelian logic intensely, then tore it apart and constructed their own methodology: the inductive method, based on the Quran and Sunnah. This lesson explores that response and the characteristics of the inductive method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Muslim community's action
What did the Muslims do with Aristotelian logic? The author says 'تناولت هذا المنطق الارسططاليسي بالدراسة والتمحيص فمزقته كل ممزق' – they studied and scrutinized it, tearing it apart.
2
Identify the outcome
What did they develop as a replacement? The author states they 'وضعوا منطقاً جديداً أو منهجاً جديداً – هو المنطق أو المنهج الإستقرائي'.
This is the inductive logic or method.
3
Identify the basis of the new method
What is the foundation of this inductive method? The author says it was based on the Quran and Sunnah from the beginning: 'مستنداً على القرآن والسنة'.
The method is not imported but derived from Islamic sources.
4
Identify the civilizational contrast
How does the author contrast the two methods? He says each method expresses the spirit of a particular civilization, with features differing greatly.
Aristotelian logic reflects Greek civilization; the inductive method reflects Islamic civilization.

وأنا أعلم أن « روزبه » القديم - عبد الله بن المقفع - وكان أكبر ضاغن على الإسلام في القديم ، قدم أول ما قدم للقضاء على نظام الإسلام الاجتماعي - كتاب مزدك ، ثم كتب باب برزويه ليثبت تناقض الأديان - وبخاصة الإسلام - وعدم يقينيتها وما يظهر له فيها من تناقض بينما يؤكد يقينية الفلسفة ووصولها الى الحق المطلق . ثم قدم أو دفع ابنه محمد بن عبد الله بن المقفع ليقدم أول ترجمة لعلم ظن أنه الصورة الكبرى لليقين قانون بديهي في نظره ، في أفق فوق الخطأ . فاذا أعلن المسلمون أن كتابهم المقدس لا يأتيه الباطل من بين يديه ولا من خلفه ، أشار لهم إلى باب برزويه ، الذي يقرر خطأ الكتاب وتناقضه ، وأن طريق الفلسفة هو صورة طريق اليقين ، ثم يدعم كل هذا بصور من المنطق الارسططاليسي ، البناء المتكامل اليقيني في نظره . .
لقد غرس روزبه الغرس ، وأتى ثمره ، فنشأت مجامع الغنوصية الخطيرة في إثر روزبه ، كما تناول المنطق ، متفلسفة ظهروا في الإسلام ، ومجدوه ، ورفعوه فوق كل يقين . وحاولوا مزجه بكل علم إسلامي .
ولم تكن الجماعة الإسلامية غافلة عن كل هذا . فسرعان ما تناولت هذا المنطق الارسططاليسي بالدراسة والتمحيص فمزقته كل ممزق وأنشأت منهجها .
بل كان المنهج - قد تكون منذ البدء - مستنداً على القرآن والسنة ، معبراً عن روح الإسلام الحقيقي إن البعث الحقيقي للروح الإسلامية وللأمة الإسلامية هو العودة الكاملة لهذا المنهج ، هو الأخذ بنصوص القرآن والسنة والعودة الى قانونهما .
ان خلفاء روزبه كثيرون في عصرنا ، وقد تعددت أشكالهم ، وتنوعت صورهم ، ولكن هم جميعاً نسخ مشوهة منتنة لابن المقفع الكريه . ولقد فشل ابن المقفع من قبل ، وهم أيضاً فاشلون .

٨ صفر عام ١٣٨٥هـ
٨ يونيه عام ١٩٦٥م .
And I know that the ancient 'Ruzbih' - Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' - who was the greatest resentful enemy of Islam in ancient times, first presented to destroy the social system of Islam the book of Mazdak, then wrote the chapter of Barzawayh to prove the contradiction of religions - especially Islam - and their lack of certainty, and what appears to him of contradiction, while he affirms the certainty of philosophy and its attainment of absolute truth. Then he presented or pushed his son Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' to present the first translation of a science that he thought was the supreme form of certainty, a self-evident law in his view, in a horizon above error. When Muslims declared that their holy book is not approached by falsehood from before it or from behind it, he pointed them to the chapter of Barzawayh, which asserts the error and contradiction of the book, and that the path of philosophy is the image of the path of certainty, then supports all this with forms of Aristotelian logic, the complete certain structure in his view. 
Ruzbih planted the seed and it bore fruit, so dangerous gnostic circles arose after Ruzbih, and likewise pseudo-philosophers who appeared in Islam took up logic, glorified it, and elevated it above all certainty. They tried to mix it with every Islamic science. 
And the Muslim community was not heedless of all this. Soon they took up this Aristotelian logic with study and scrutiny, tearing it apart completely and establishing their own method. 
Rather, the method - perhaps it was from the beginning - was based on the Quran and Sunnah, expressing the true spirit of Islam. The true revival of the Islamic spirit and the Islamic nation is the complete return to this method, to adhering to the texts of the Quran and Sunnah and returning to their law. 
Indeed, the successors of Ruzbih are many in our time, their forms multiplied and their images varied, but they are all distorted foul copies of the odious Ibn al-Muqaffa'. And Ibn al-Muqaffa' failed before, and they too are failures. 
The objective scientific study, which I present to all researchers in this book, definitively proves that Muslims never accepted this Aristotelian syllogistic logic; rather, they attacked and criticized it with the fiercest attack and harshest criticism. Then they developed a new logic or a new methodology - that is the inductive logic or method. And each of these methods expresses the spirit of a particular civilization, with features that differ greatly from the other. 
I wrote the first version of this book in the early years of youth (1940-1942), then published it in 1947, and now I present it in a second edition, in which the basic idea has not changed, but many additions have been made to its material, yet the book retains its original character. 
Dr. Ali Sami al-Nashshar
Professor of Islamic Philosophy
Faculty of Arts - University of Alexandria
Tuesday
8 Safar 1385 AH
8 June 1965 AD.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is the author's prefatory historical and ideological introduction. It begins by identifying Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' (originally Ruzbih) as a primary enemy of Islam who first introduced Mazdak's book to undermine Islamic social order, then wrote 'Bab Barzawayh' to claim contradictions in religions (especially Islam) while asserting philosophy's absolute certainty. He then had his son translate a work of logic, considering it the supreme form of certainty. When Muslims asserted the Quran's inerrancy, Ibn al-Muqaffa' used Bab Barzawayh to argue for the Bible's corruption and philosophy's superiority, supported by Aristotelian logic. The author then states that Ruzbih's efforts bore fruit in dangerous gnostic circles and pseudo-philosophers within Islam who glorified logic and tried to merge it with Islamic sciences. However, the Muslim community responded by scrutinizing and tearing apart Aristotelian logic, establishing their own method based on the Quran and Sunnah. The author asserts that true revival lies in returning to this method. He compares contemporary enemies to Ibn al-Muqaffa', declaring them failures. He then claims his study proves Muslims never accepted Aristotelian syllogistic logic; rather, they criticized it and developed an inductive method, each method reflecting a distinct civilizational spirit. Finally, he notes that this second edition retains the original idea with added material. The tone is polemical and patriotic, setting the stage for his own methodology.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Al-Nashar's Thesis: Muslim Rejection of Aristotelian Logic
Author states his thesis: Muslims rejected Aristotelian logic and created inductive logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate al-Nashar's central thesis that Muslims rejected Aristotelian syllogistic logic and created an inductive method, and contrast it with the standard narrative of Muslim reception of Greek logic.

Core Idea
Muslims did not adopt Aristotle's logic; they built their own inductive method.

The author, Ali Sami al-Nashar, opens the second edition of his book with a bold historical claim. He states that his impartial study proves that Muslims never accepted Aristotelian syllogistic logic but instead attacked it and created a new inductive logic. This thesis challenges the common view that Muslims simply preserved and transmitted Greek logic. Understanding this claim is essential for grasping the book's argument about the distinctiveness of Islamic civilization's intellectual approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's main claim
Read the first two sentences of the passage. The author says Muslims 'never accepted' Aristotelian syllogistic logic, but rather 'attacked and criticized it' and then 'established a new logic or method' — the inductive method. Write down this thesis in your own words.
2
Contrast the two logical systems
Notice that the author contrasts 'this Aristotelian syllogistic logic' with 'the inductive logic or method.' He also adds that each method 'expresses the spirit of a particular civilization.' This implies that logic is culturally shaped, not purely universal. Consider how this contrast frames the rest of the book.
The term 'qiyas' in the passage refers to syllogism, not analogical reasoning (as in fiqh).
3
Contextualize the author's autobiography
The author mentions writing the first version in his early youth (1940-1942) and publishing it in 1947. The second edition adds material but keeps the 'fundamental idea.' This shows the thesis is long-held and central to his scholarly identity. Reflect on how a scholar's personal journey might shape a revisionist claim.

The impartial scientific study, which I present to all researchers in this book, conclusively proves that the Muslims never accepted this Aristotelian syllogistic logic; rather, they attacked it and criticized it with the most severe attacks and harshest criticism. Then they established a new logic or a new method — the inductive logic or method. Each of these methods expresses the spirit of a particular civilization, whose features differ most extremely from the other. I wrote the first version of this book in my early youth (1940-1942), then published it in 1947. Now I present it in a second edition; the fundamental idea has not changed, but many additions have been made to its material, yet the book still retains its original basic character. Dr. Ali Sami al-Nashar Professor of Islamic Philosophy Faculty of Arts - Alexandria University Tuesday 8 Safar 1385 AH / 8 June 1965 AD.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to the second edition. It opens with a strong claim: the impartial scientific study in this book proves that Muslims never accepted Aristotelian syllogistic logic. Instead, they attacked and criticized it severely, and then created a new inductive logic/method. The author contrasts this with the usual narrative. He then provides a brief history: the first version was written in his early youth (1940-1942) and published in 1947. The second edition retains the core idea but adds much new material. The passage concludes with the author's name and date. The core argument is historical and methodological: Islamic civilization developed its own distinctive approach to logic.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Myth of the 'Greek Seduction'
Author challenges prevailing view on Aristotelian logic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two competing narratives about the reception of Aristotelian logic in Islam and articulate the author's revisionist position.

Core Idea
The 'Greek seduction' is a myth; Islam sharply rejected Greek philosophical methods.

This passage opens the first edition of a work that aims to overturn a long-held assumption among scholars. The author describes how both Eastern and Western researchers believed that Aristotelian logic was warmly embraced by Islamic civilization and became the unchallenged standard of reason. He then reveals his own skepticism after deep study, arguing that this logic is inseparable from Greek philosophy, which Islam vigorously opposed. Understanding his argument helps us see the stakes in recovering an authentic Islamic approach to logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prevailing view
Read the first lines describing what researchers believed: that Aristotelian logic received 'the best reception' and was considered 'the undisputable law of the intellect' and 'the fixed scientific method'. Notice how the author lists the elements: definitions, propositions, syllogisms.
This view is what the author is challenging.
2
Spot the author's shift in stance
After presenting the common view, the author writes 'I stood before this idea... in a position of doubt and suspicion.' This is the pivot point. Observe his word choice: 'shakk' (doubt) and 'irtiyāb' (suspicion).
The author's tone changes from descriptive to critical.
3
Extract the author's reasons for doubt
The author gives two main reasons: (1) Aristotelian logic is intimately connected to Greek intellectual sciences, especially philosophy; (2) It is the most precise expression of the Greek spirit. Then he asserts that Islam rejected Greek intellectual sciences harshly.
The author presents these as factual claims, not just opinions.
4
Consider the implication
If Islam rejected Greek sciences, then the idea that Muslims wholeheartedly adopted Aristotelian logic cannot hold. The author implies that the 'Greek seduction' narrative is a scholarly invention that needs to be re-examined.
The passage is cut off mid-sentence, so the full argument continues.

تَصْدِيرُ الطَّبْعَةِ الأولى كانت الفكرة السائدة لدى الباحثين - شرقيين وأوروبيين - أن المنطق الارسططاليسي قوبل في العالم الإسلامي - حين ترجم وتوالت تراجمه - أحسن مقابلة . فسرعان ما اعتبرته المدارس الإسلامية - على اختلاف نزعاتها وتباين أغراضها - قانون العقل الذي لا يرد ، والمنهج العلمي الثابت . تعاريفه وحدوده ثابتة . وأحكامه وقضاياه مسلمة . وأقيسته منتجة لليقين وموصلة إلى العلم من حيث هو . ومن ثمة نشأت تلك الفكرة القائلة : إن المنطق الأرسططاليسي أميز مثال « للفتنة اليونانية » التي افتتن بها المسلمون ، والتي سيطرت على عقولهم حتى العصور القريبة . وبهذا حل الباحثون مشكلة المنهج في العالم الإسلامي . إن هذا المنهج كان أرسططاليسياً ، إن في كلياته وإن في تفصيلاته . وقفت أمام هذه الفكرة - بعد دراسة عميقة للمنطق الارسططاليسي - موقف الشك والارتياب إن هذا المنطق هو منهج البحث في علوم اليونان الفكرية والفلسفية منها على الخصوص . يتصل بها أوثق اتصال وتختلط أبحاثه وتتشابك بأبحاثها . ثم إن هذا المنطق هو أدق تعبير عن الروح اليونانية في نظرتها إلى الكون وفي محاولتها إقامة مذاهبها في الوجود . وقد لفظ الإسلام علوم اليونان الفكرية لفظاً قاسياً . وحاربها أشد محاربة - كانت الروح
Preface to the First Edition: The prevailing idea among researchers - Eastern and European - was that Aristotelian logic was received in the Islamic world, when it was translated and its translations multiplied, with the best reception. Soon Islamic schools, despite their different inclinations and diverse aims, considered it the indisputable law of the intellect and the fixed scientific method. Its definitions and limits were fixed. Its propositions and judgments were accepted. Its syllogisms produced certainty and led to knowledge as such. Hence arose the idea that Aristotelian logic is the most distinguished example of the 'Greek seduction' that fascinated Muslims and dominated their minds until recent times. And thus researchers solved the problem of method in the Islamic world. This method was Aristotelian, both in its universals and its particulars. I stood before this idea - after deep study of Aristotelian logic - in a position of doubt and suspicion that this logic is the method of research in the intellectual sciences of the Greeks, especially philosophical ones. It is connected to them with the closest connection, and its investigations are mixed and intertwined with theirs. Moreover, this logic is the most precise expression of the Greek spirit in its view of the universe and in its attempt to establish its doctrines about existence. And Islam rejected the intellectual sciences of the Greeks with a harsh rejection. And it fought them with the most severe fighting - it was the spirit
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is the preface to the first edition. The author begins by describing the prevailing view among both Eastern and Western researchers: that Aristotelian logic was well-received in the Islamic world, considered the indisputable law of reason and the fixed scientific method. Its definitions, propositions, and syllogisms were accepted as productive of certainty. This led to the idea that Aristotelian logic is the prime example of the 'Greek seduction' that fascinated Muslims until recent times, and thus the method problem was solved: it was Aristotelian in all respects. The author then states his own position: after deep study, he stood in doubt and suspicion. He argues that this logic is intimately connected to Greek intellectual sciences, particularly philosophy, and is the exact expression of the Greek spirit. Finally, he asserts that Islam rejected these Greek intellectual sciences harshly and fought them severely. The sentence cuts off with 'it was the spirit,' implying a conclusion that the spirit of Greek thought is incompatible with Islam.

Key Terms
الفتنة اليونانية
القانون العقل
المنهج العلمي الثابت

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It was ignored.
D) It was modified into inductive logic.

Key Takeaway
The author challenges the myth of the 'Greek seduction' by arguing that Islam rejected Greek sciences, thus undermining the idea that Aristotelian logic dominated Islamic thought.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Author's Thesis: An Independent Islamic Methodology
Author's preface critiquing the 'Greek seduction' thesis and proposing an Islamic alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's central claim and distinguish his proposed sources for Islamic methodology from the prevailing view of Aristotelian adoption.

Core Idea
Islamic methodology is not imported Greek logic but an original empirical method from within Islamic civilization.

This preface launches the book by challenging a deeply held assumption: that Islamic scholarship uncritically adopted Aristotelian logic. The author positions himself as a skeptic who, after deep study, argues that Islam's unique spirit and sciences necessitated a distinct methodological framework. He then reveals his discovery of that framework in the works of jurists, usul scholars, and theologians.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prevailing view
Read the first paragraph: what does the author say most researchers believed about Aristotelian logic and the Islamic world?
They thought it was accepted as the unchallenged law of reason.
2
Spot the author's challenge
Find the sentence where the author states his position of doubt and suspicion after studying Aristotelian logic.
He argues that this logic is inseparably tied to Greek philosophy, which Islam rejected.
3
Extract the author's positive claim
Identify what the author proposes as an alternative: an Islamic methodology derived from which sources?
From jurists, usul scholars, theologians, not from 'Philosophers of Islam'.
4
Understand the historical assertion
The author claims that this Islamic empirical method was later 'discovered' by Europeans. What does he imply about precedence?
Muslims preceded modern Europeans in developing the empirical method.
